## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration over time. The rate dA_dt is expected to follow a rate law depending on concentration A, and possibly explicitly on time t for driven/non-autonomous systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Reversible second-order/first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate law from complex mechanism)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed conversion)
- Cubic autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)**2 (higher-order autocatalytic mechanism)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing first and second order pathways)
- Saturation kinetics (non-Michaelis form): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) (substrate inhibition or complex mechanism)
- Time-dependent forcing with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (driven reaction system)
- Fractional order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (sum of fractional-order terms)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (general cubic mechanism from mass-action kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → autonomous ODE rate law, suggests closed chemical system with mass-action kinetics
- Negative rate proportional to A^n → simple consumption/decay reaction of order n
- Quadratic terms in A with opposite signs → reversible or competing reactions with equilibrium point
- Product of A and (constant - A) → conservation law constraint where total concentration is fixed, typical of A ↔ B systems
- Cubic terms in concentration → trimolecular reactions or complex mechanisms with intermediate species eliminated
- Rational functions of A → quasi-steady-state approximation applied to intermediate species in enzyme or catalytic mechanisms
- Explicit time dependence → non-autonomous system such as photolysis, temperature ramp, or external reagent addition
- Multiple stable/unstable fixed points in dA_dt vs A → bistable chemical switch or ignition-extinction behavior
- Rate law with both positive and negative powers of A → complex catalytic cycle with inhibition and activation
